[0]The Tinellbian Languages Dictionary
<h2>About</h2>
    <p class="introduction">This dictionary aims to describe all the vocabulary items of the twenty Tinellbian languages, consisting of High Lulani and its descendants. In addition, miscellaneous English neologisms have been added, including proper nouns.</p>
    <div class="search-box" id="word-search-box">
      <h2>Searching</h2>
      <input type="text" name="search" id="wordsearch" onKeyDown="if (event.keyCode == 13) {dictionarysearch()}">
      <input type="button" name="dictionary" id="dictionary" onClick="dictionarysearch()" value="Jump to Entry">
    <p class="introduction">The search box directly above allows one to proceed directly to any dictionary entry. Contrariwise, the search box in the navigation pane runs a general search of the site.</p>

1]-&#x294;a
[2]High Lulani
[3]<high-lulani>\(;a\)</high-lulani>
[4]<ipa><a href="http://grammar.tinellb.com/highlulani/phonology/index.html">/&#x294;.j&#x259;/</a></ipa>
[5]particle <div class="definition"><em>(indicates emphasis)</em>
[6]Usage Notes
[l]Placed at the end of greetings and salutations.
Often elided, moving the stress of the last word to the final syllable.[/l]
[6]Example
N&agrave;ra &rarr; Nar&agrave;&#x294;a &rarr; Nar&agrave; <em>goodbye!</em>&date=20180118--------------------------------------------------2

[6]Usage Notes
these are just about the only terms of this type. Anything else uses the genitive.
[6]Examples
<strong>daqa &rsquo;ala</strong>
<high-lulani>(dq / al)</high-lulani>
<em>water-<small-caps>gen</small-caps> heat</em>

[5]abstract stem count <a href="http://grammar.tinellb.com/highlulani/morphology/nouns.html">noun</a> <div class="definition">temperature degree</div>
[6]Notes*
This temperature scale is set with <strong>0</strong> <em>0</em> at absolute zero, and <strong>495</strong> <em>230</em> at the triple point of water.
In ordinary use, temperatures between <strong>450</strong> <em>200</em> and <strong>675</strong> <em>300</em> are given without the hundreds place.
<p class="note">*Numbers in <strong>bold</strong> are in decimal, numbers in <em>italics</em> are in balanced <a href="../s/sesquidecimal.html">sesquidecimal</a>.</p>

<em>cat</em> <small-caps>dat-</small-caps><em>dog change.</em>
&ldquo;The cat became a dog.&rdquo;

[1]bitta
[2]High Lulani
[3]<high-lulani>(B;t)</high-lulani>
[4]<ipa><a href="http://grammar.tinellb.com/highlulani/phonology/index.html">/&#x2c8;bit.t&#x259;/</a></ipa>
[5]inanimate stem <a href="http://grammar.tinellb.com/highlulani/morphology/nouns.html">noun</a> <div class="definition">time</div>
[6]Definition
the two temporal dimensions
[6]Notes
The first dimension of time is subjective: a person's birth is <em>before</em> their death.
The second dimension is objective: if one time-travels into the past, then one's death may well be <em>upstream</em> of one's birth.
[6]Derived Terms
<strong><a href="../j/jannibitta.html">jannibitta</a></strong> <high-lulani>(j;NB;t)</high-lulani> <em>to time travel</em>
[6]Hypernym
<strong><a href="../c/calu.html">calu</a></strong> <high-lulani>(cW)</high-lulani> <em>dimension</em>
[6]See Also
<strong><a href="../u/'u'ili.html">&rsquo;u&rsquo;ili</a></strong> <high-lulani>(uiL)</high-lulani> <em>reality</em>
<strong><a href="../s/sufi.html">sufi</a></strong> <high-lulani>(zF)</high-lulani> <em>space</em>
<strong><a href="../m/ma''u.html">ma&#x294;u</a></strong> <high-lulani>(m;u)</high-lulani> <em>gingla</em>

[1]bunali
[2]High Lulani
[3]<high-lulani>(OnL)</high-lulani>
[4]<ipa><a href="http://grammar.tinellb.com/highlulani/phonology/index.html">/b&#x289;.&#x2c8;nal.&#x268;/</a></ipa>
[5]abstract stem <a href="http://grammar.tinellb.com/highlulani/morphology/nouns.html">noun</a> <div class="definition">rhyme; assonance</div>
[6]Definition
to have the same vowels and placement of geminates
[6]Examples
[e](These are perhaps nonsense words, to demonstrate <strong>bunali</strong>)

<strong>kana / lara</strong>
<strong>biru / kitu</strong>
<strong>kippu / lirru</strong>
[6]Non-examples

<strong>kiru / kirru</strong> - <em>different geminate placement</em>&date=20171231

[1]gingla
[2]English
[3]
[4]<ipa>/&#x2c8;gi&#x14b;.gl&#x259;/</ipa>
[5]abstract stem noun <div class="definition">planes of existence; ghostly realms</div>
[6]Definition
there are four ginglaic dimensions. These correspond to the seven planes in some esoteric systems, or to otherworldly realms, <em>i.e.:</em> in order to explain paranormal events.
[6]Notes
<a href="../x/xaraduluri.html">Xaraduluri</a> are capable of moving through <em>gingla</em>

[1]musaqapi
[2]High Lulani
[3]<high-lulani>(UsqP)</high-lulani>
[4]<ipa><a href="http://grammar.tinellb.com/highlulani/phonology/index.html">/&#x2cc;mus.&#x259;.&#x2c8;&#x14b;ap&#x2b0;.&#x268;/</a></ipa>
[5]abstract derived compound <a href="http://grammar.tinellb.com/highlulani/morphology/nouns.html">noun</a> <div class="definition">week</div>
[6]Etymology
<strong><a href="../m/musa.html">musa</a></strong> <high-lulani>(Us)</high-lulani> <em>day</em> + <strong><a href="../q/qapi.html">qapi</a></strong> <high-lulani>(qP)</high-lulani> <em>chain</em>
[6]Notes
while the week of native High Lulani speakers consisted of nine days, this word is used to refer to any similar period of time

[5]<a href="http://grammar.tinellb.com/highlulani/morphology/verbs.html#transitivity">intransitive</a> stem <a href="http://grammar.tinellb.com/highlulani/morphology/verbs.html">verb</a> <div class="definition">to be ready; to be completed; to be prepared</div>
[6]Thematic Roles
<strong>patient</strong> <em>subject</em>
<strong>agent</strong> <em>ablative</em>
[6]Example
<strong>&#x294;usu suqapakka si&rsquo;apa.</strong>
<high-lulani>(.uz / zqp;k / Sap.)</high-lulani>
<small-caps>1int</small-caps> <em>prepare-</em><small-caps>abp</small-caps> <em>meal.</em>
&ldquo;I prepared the meal.&rdquo;
[6]Notes
the patient must be inanimate.

[4]<ipa><a href="http://grammar.tinellb.com/highlulani/phonology/index.html">/&#x255;u&#x2d0;/</a></ipa>
[5]stem transitive <a href="http://grammar.tinellb.com/highlulani/morphology/verbs.html">verb</a> <div class="definition">to put out; to radiate; to broadcast</div>
[6]Thematic Relations
<strong>stimulus</strong> <em>subject</em>
<strong>experiencer</strong> <em>dative</em>
<strong>theme</strong> <em>object</em>, <small-caps>ka</small-caps>
[6]Usage Notes
inanimate themes are objects, animate themes use <small-caps>ka</small-caps>
[6]Examples
<strong>Filli pixi xusina.</strong>
<high-lulani>.F;L / PX / ZSn.</high-lulani>
<small-caps>2int 1dat seem-beauty.</small-caps>
&ldquo;You seem pretty to me.&rdquo;
[f]<strong>Filli ka-&rsquo;aggami.</strong>
<high-lulani>.F;L / ka;gM.</high-lulani>
<em><small-caps>2int</small-caps> as-policeman.</em>
&ldquo;You look like a policeman.&rdquo;
[6]Notes

[5]derived compound <a href="http://grammar.tinellb.com/highlulani/morphology/nouns.html">noun</a> <div class="definition">elder</div>
